Special Item

The Feetham Report, Volume II (Continued, Part 6) 213

Abstract Translation of the Fourth and Fifth Sections: The current governing system of the Public Concession, established according to the Land Regulations, is a most direct form of democracy, as stated above. The participation of Chinese people in the representative system of the Public Concession is still in its infancy. The considerations mentioned above indicate that, from the perspective of public interest, it would be unfair to Chinese society to suddenly have Chinese representatives assume the majority of responsibilities in the existing administrative system of the Public Concession. Chinese voters must have adequate opportunities to become familiar with public elections and discover the best methods of election. Both voters and representatives must also have opportunities to learn more about the nature of the work undertaken by the board of directors and the relationship of individual elected officials to the members of a public body. The special nature and value of the Public Concession's administration come from inherited customs and standards. If these customs and standards are to be preserved, then the responsibility for all major positions in the Public Concession service must be transferred from foreign directors to Chinese directors slowly and gradually. The renowned writer John Stuart Mill said, "The nature and extent of the authority exercised over the individual, the distribution of powers, and the conditions of commanding and obeying are the most powerful of all influences. Except for the individual's religious beliefs, only these influences can create the individual as he is now and make him what he can become." If this statement is true, then when a people begin to participate in a representative system they have never fully experienced, they must be given time for this system to exert its influence as "a great force influencing human thought." Only then can the new participants be prepared to take over this representative system. Based on the above reasons, I have concluded that the number of Chinese directors should not be increased to the point where they constitute a majority on the board. I also do not believe it is appropriate to increase the number of Chinese directors to be nearly equal to the number of foreign directors. Such a method may give rise to power struggles and, as can be imagined, may even open up paths to undesirable conspiracies. However, if the total number of board members is increased according to the following recommendations, then I believe that the number of Chinese directors should be increased such that: (a) in terms of the proportion of the total number of directors, the proportion of Chinese directors in the future should not be less than the current proportion of Chinese directors; (b) the number of Chinese directors may be greater than the number of directors of any other nationality. Adopting this distribution basis means that the number of Chinese directors will always be more than one-third of the total number of directors on the board. Although the portion of the residents of the Public Concession represented by Chinese directors is far larger than other parts, Chinese directors still constitute a minority on the board. In this regard, whether any special provisions are necessary to clearly protect the interests of the Chinese people is a question to be considered separately. The main goals that should always be kept in mind for any plan to reform the existing Public Concession organization law are as follows: (1) So-called international cooperation refers to (a) cooperation between Chinese and foreigners, and (b) cooperation between representatives of various nationalities that make up the foreign community. To expand the foundation of international cooperation on which the Public Concession governance system relies and to increase its strength, and to establish a suitable organizational function for this expansion and increase in strength. (2) To define all general powers possessed by the Public Concession's governing body, the Shanghai Municipal Council, in wording that allows these powers to be exercised effectively and without doubt within its scope, thereby eliminating all causes of conflict and facilitating cooperation between the Municipal Council and the Chinese authorities. (3) To ensure that any method or limit of constitutional change is suitable for the protection of the principles of autonomy and rule of law on which the current governing system of the Public Concession is based, and suitable for maintaining and improving the general standards of administrative efficiency of the Public Concession, with particular attention to the security of Chinese and foreign residents or merchants within the Public Concession. (4) To adopt more effective methods of publication so that an enlightened public opinion can develop throughout the society of the Public Concession. The basis of this public opinion is twofold: on the one hand, a clear understanding of the common interests and responsibilities of the residents of all countries that make up the Public Concession, and on the other hand, a better understanding of the scope and nature of the tasks and capabilities of the Municipal Council, the governing body of the Public Concession. In this way, the Municipal Council can more fully rely on the practical assistance of all parts of the population when exercising its powers in a clear and decisive manner. Regarding the reform plans for the Ratepayers' Meeting and the Shanghai Municipal Council, the following recommendations are made: 1. The Ratepayers' Meeting should hold two types of Ratepayers' Meetings, one representing foreign ratepayers and one representing Chinese ratepayers, to replace the foreign ratepayers' annual meeting stipulated in Articles 9 and 19 of the Land Regulations. All proposals submitted to the foreign ratepayers' annual meeting for deliberation according to existing regulations should be submitted separately to the Chinese and foreign Ratepayers' Meetings for decision. If a special motion is adopted by both meetings, then their joint resolution will take effect. However, if the resolutions of the two Ratepayers' Meetings differ, then the resolutions of both parties should only be regarded as a kind of consultative nature. The decision should be referred to the board of directors, but the board of directors must review the issue again in accordance with the proceedings of the two meetings and their decisions before making a final decision. For example, if the budget is passed by both the Chinese and foreign Ratepayers' Meetings as proposed, or if it is passed by both meetings with the same restrictions, then the budget passed in this way will be the final budget. However, if one meeting passes a proposal to increase or decrease expenditure that is rejected by the other meeting, then whether the expenditure should be increased or decreased should be decided by the board of directors with reference to the discussions and decisions of the two meetings. The same method applies to proposals for levying taxes. Before adopting a plan to establish a foreign ratepayers' representative body to replace the existing foreign ratepayers' meeting, the foreign ratepayers' meeting should still be a general meeting that all foreigners who meet the qualifications stipulated in the existing Land Regulations can attend. Any such plan that is not included in the Land Regulations should first be submitted by the board of directors to the foreign ratepayers' meeting for deliberation and then implemented. The Chinese Ratepayers' Meeting is a meeting of a representative body. The election of this representative body should be conducted in accordance with a plan proposed by the Chinese directors and approved by the board of directors. The above recommendations, except where the same proposal is unanimously passed by both the Chinese and foreign Ratepayers' Meetings, should only be regarded as a kind of consultative nature. This recommendation is subject to the following restriction: the Shanghai Municipal Council shall not increase taxes (especially land tax and house tax) beyond a certain standard without first obtaining the consent of both Ratepayers' Meetings. Any tax increase proposal exceeding this standard may be vetoed by both Ratepayers' Meetings. However, this restriction should not be worded in such a way that the Shanghai Municipal Council is not allowed to implement any tax increase exceeding the current standard without the consent of both Ratepayers' Meetings. More room for increase should be left above the current tax rates. The election of auditors and property committee members by both Ratepayers' Meetings has also been discussed and recommended. These personnel should be elected separately by the two Ratepayers' Meetings. 2. The power to make by-laws should belong to the board of directors in the future, not to special meetings of taxpayers. The quorum for this meeting is stipulated in Article 11 of the Land Regulations. However, three months before the Shanghai Municipal Council makes any by-laws, it should publish the proposed by-laws in the Municipal Council Gazette so that those who oppose their implementation have ample opportunity to make representations. 3. Increase the number of directors to expand the board of directors so that all directors are at least twenty-two and no more than thirty. The number of directors may be increased in stages. The first stage should increase to twenty-two, and then continue to increase. If all Chinese directors are increased in this way, as mentioned above, then the proportion of Chinese directors should not be less than the current proportion of Chinese directors in terms of the proportion of the total number of directors, and the number of Chinese directors may be greater than the number of directors of any other nationality. 4. Electoral Law (a) Foreign Directors: For foreign directors, the current electoral system must be modified to provide that two different electoral laws will be adopted in the future. Some foreign directors will be elected by individual foreign taxpayers as they are now. Some will be elected by chambers of commerce or other similar bodies representing foreign nationalities. However, how the foreign directors elected by the proposed chambers of commerce or other national bodies represent each nationality should be specified. As for the directors elected by foreign taxpayers, it should also be stipulated that each of the three foreign countries represented by the current directors of the board must retain a certain number of seats. (b) Chinese Directors: The method of electing Chinese directors is the same as the method of electing foreign directors. That is, when a public election system can be adopted, some Chinese directors should be elected by individual Chinese taxpayers, and some should be elected by Chinese bodies. However, before a public election method for Chinese directors can be adopted, the method of election by Chinese bodies should continue to be handled by the Chinese Ratepayers' Association or other appropriate bodies. However, it should be amended when it is deemed appropriate to ensure that all elected Chinese directors can include the Chinese directors who can be elected in the last public election. The reasons for the third recommendation to increase the number of directors and the fourth recommendation to change the electoral method have been explained and instructed as follows: Now that the board of directors has been granted broader and more independent powers, including legislative powers, the number of directors should be increased in order to enable the council to more fully represent the entire body of residents.

A Small Chronicle of the World 215

— Sea Guest

Children's Favorite Movies

The teachers at a school in Dumfries, England, noting the students' enthusiasm for watching movies, posed a question to them asking what kind of movies they liked to watch. Ninety-eight percent of the male students replied that they liked watching romance movies. Ninety-four percent of the female students replied that they liked watching military murder cases, struggles, and the like.

Houses Deep Underground

American houses strive to be tall and reach the sky, while Japanese houses strive to be deep underground. Why do they want to go deep underground? Because there are too many earthquakes. It is said that in the center of Tokyo, there are plans to build such a deep house, going eighty stories deep underground and capable of being added to at any time as needed. It will be made entirely of steel, reinforced concrete, and stone, forming a cylindrical shape 155 feet in diameter and 1,100 feet deep, with a circular ventilation tunnel 75 feet in diameter running straight through the house to eliminate any stuffiness. All modern equipment such as electric lights, telephones, radios, elevators, and sunlight reflectors will be fully equipped. It is said that the construction time will be half of what it would take to build a 50-story building, and the construction cost will be approximately 2.5 million pounds. If this plan is realized, then no matter how severe the earthquake in Tokyo, this house will be unaffected.

Remembering Dr. Richard Wilhelm, Famous German Sinologist 216

— Xu Shiqi

Since Western material civilization has surged eastward, our countrymen have tended towards industrialization and mechanization, discarding national traditions and abandoning our inherent civilization. They have failed to understand that spiritual and material things must be balanced. Deformed development only increases harm. Germany has long been known for its scientific achievements and holds a leading position in the world. Recently, with overproduction and worker unemployment, it is about to lead to a trend where humanity is driven and oppressed by material things, gradually evolving into a situation of overthrow, collapse, and terror. Scholars across the country advocate introducing Eastern civilization to correct this drawback. However, Sinology is difficult and different from Latin. Without a special research institution, it would be impossible to gain insight into its depths.

This spring, I traveled to Frankfurt, Germany, on business and had the opportunity to visit the local Chinese Academy. I learned about the spirit of Dr. Richard Wilhelm, the former president of the academy, in his study of Sinology and the regret after his death. Therefore, I record his biography to warn those in our country who dabble in Western learning while abandoning national traditions.

Dr. Wilhelm was born in 1873 and died at the age of 57. He graduated from the University of Tübingen and the Stift Theological Seminary. He lived in China for 25 years, serving as a pastor in Qingdao, running schools and hospitals, and passionately pursuing Sinology. He associated with Gu Hongming, Kang Nanhai, Liang Rengong, and others. He once served as a professor at Peking University and wrote extensively. He translated the Analects, Mencius, the Tao Te Ching, the Liezi, the Zhuangzi, and other books into German, and wrote "The Soul of China" (Die Seele Chinas), elucidating the inherent civilization of the East and his personal views on China in order to introduce it to German youth and correct European misconceptions about China. This had a huge impact. Today, major universities in various German cities have added Chinese language departments, and the Dr. was an influential figure for this.

In 1924, Dr. Wilhelm was hired by the University of Frankfurt to lecture on the origin of Chinese characters and Chinese culture. At the same time, he founded the Chinese Academy to provide Germans with the opportunity to study Sinology in depth. He wrote "A History of Chinese Literature," "A History of Chinese Philosophy," and "A History of Chinese Culture," and traveled throughout Europe lecturing on Chinese cultural issues. The academy invited Chinese scholars to give lectures, including Dr. Hu Shih.

Due to overwork, Dr. Wilhelm died of illness in Frankfurt on March 6, 1930. His wife, Mrs. BlueHart, bore him four children. She was gentle and virtuous. Dr. Wilhelm's last major work, "Chinese Religion and Philosophy," was not completed. However, although Dr. Wilhelm passed away, his special spirit has permeated throughout Europe.

Among the Westerners who have traveled to China and studied Sinology extensively, the one I know is the late American Dr. Li Jiabai, who lived in Shanghai for nearly 30 years and founded the Shangxian Hall on Songshan Road to engage in charitable undertakings. He associated with famous scholars in the country and translated and wrote extensively, also composing poetry and lyrics, which were remarkable and unique in style. Unfortunately, I am forgetful and cannot recall the successive passing of those great talents. It is truly lamentable.

In early summer of the year Xinwei (1931), Elder Sun Shoushi and Elder Yao Jinqiu invited the poets of the Mingshe for a tour of Mount Zhidou. The pomegranate flowers were in full bloom, tens of thousands of them stretching for four or five li, creating a magnificent spectacle. I wrote a long poem to commemorate it. 217

— Zheng Zhian

The flower season in Jiangnan in April is over, and searching for flowers only brings thoughts of spring. Going out for a tour feels lost, as if something is missing. What shall we do with wine? We specially go through the prefectural government to Mount Zhidou. The path is narrow and the carriage struggles. How do we know there is another world, where the peaks turn and the heart opens? The fire on the branches is first seen, and the red flowers are enough to delight the eyes. In an instant, the prairie fire spreads, blazing and boundless, how can it be exhausted? Three or five li, all are red. Thousands and thousands of trees are coral red. Who got the excellent varieties of the forest and planted them here? Don't say this color is empty, don't say that city is a torch, the ashes have not died, flying into the empty valley, still raging. It's like the evening glow of Chicheng rising, its splendor stretching across the sky, baking the great river and overturning the father's shadow, as if a winding dragon is coming to light the way. The red frost has not melted, spewing out wild floods, the empty mountain turns over the south wind morning and evening. Leaning on the wind, I want to shout "stone vinegar, stone vinegar!" What is the joy here like? In the ten thousand greens, a red spot, Jinggong already praised it back then. Moreover, looking at the red road, the carriages are like fish entering it. Looking at the flowers, we do not think of attaching to the heat. How do we know the sorrows of the mountain? There is such happiness in the world, is it the same as the Peach Blossom Spring? If we are written into a picture, the flushed faces should be thicker than the mountain mist. The pomegranate fields have long been famous because of Fan Xie's writing, truly human effort is not the work of nature. Who gave a branch to Lanqi? For no reason, I think of Mount Dong.

A Record of Shi Guzi's Painting of Horses 218

— Chen Boying

Shi Guzi's painting of horses is a long scroll on silk, ten and a half inches high and one hundred and ninety-eight inches long. On the right end, there are two large trees and four small trees extending horizontally. Behind them are many slender bamboos along the shore. Across the bank are seven or eight small stones. A horse stands to the left of the trees, raising its foot as if to walk. To the left of the horse, there is another clump of trees covering the river surface. Further to the left, the water ripples gently. A horse crouches in an open area, gnawing at its hooves. Across the bank, there is a continent with five trees, only their roots visible. Then three trees with only half their trunks showing, and a short tree like a child reaching under an adult's armpit, stretching its head out. Reeds and rushes grow far and near along the water's edge. There is another horse turning its head to the right, looking back while gnawing at its hooves. Beside it, there is a herd of horses. One horse stands facing left, one horse behind it wanting to come forward, and one horse stands forward. There is another horse standing sideways. Further to the left, a person is pulling a horse across the river, but the horse refuses to move, raising its front hooves to kick. The person is about five or six feet away from the horse, and the water reaches his shins. At this point, the land ends, and the water gradually widens. There are only eight or nine old tree roots along the bank, and a dozen or so scattered stones by the water's edge. The ripples are like scattered water, with shimmering reflections. Two people each sit on a horse halfway across the river. The former reins in his horse to stop and talk, while the latter leans forward, tilting his ear to listen. Further to the left, one horse has both feet on land and is starting to rise. Slightly further away, a person is scooping water to wash a horse. Another horse is also in the water, as if it has already been washed. On the bank, there is a horse sitting and stretching. Slightly past two large trees, one covered in dense dead vines, and the other behind, there is a rocky cliff where the water reaches. Under the trees, two horses squat, one facing the trees and looking left. The eyes of the two horses are each focused. To the left of the trees, one horse lies on the ground rolling, its belly facing up and all four feet raised. A horse stands beside it, as if lost in thought. Another horse bows its head, gnawing at its shin. Two horses sit on the left and right of the trees. The horse on the right sits with its back facing the trees. Slightly forward, a horse is leaping. Another herd of horses is walking under pine trees. One horse is gnawing at its horseshoe, one horse leans its head on the pine tree to rub, one horse follows behind it, and one horse has already turned around, still looking forward. Two horses bow their heads, wanting to eat grass. A young horse follows at the end. Beside the pines, there are three other horses, one standing tall, one rubbing its neck, and one bowing its head to look down. There is another horse standing separately under a pine tree. Further to the left, one horse turns its head to play with its tail. Two horses walk to the right, side by side, talking to each other. Behind them, there is a small stream with three bends, the spring flowing continuously. From there to the end, a level slope can be seen. In the distance, slender bamboos are planted densely. Nearby, there are two or three large stones with several clumps of bamboo growing on them. There are several lines of geese flying from the left. Inscribed on the painting: "In the winter month of Wuzi, imitating the brushstrokes of Zhao Jixian, painted by Wang Hui, Shigu Zi of Yushan." Seals with the red characters "Wang Hui zhi Yin" (Seal of Wang Hui). In total, there are four people and thirty-seven horses, all painted in color with meticulous brushstrokes. According to Shigu, his other name is Gengyan, and he is as famous as Lutai and Yuanzhao, known as the "Four Wangs." He excels at painting landscapes. His works include "Peach Blossom Spring," "Autumn Colors of Dongting," "Bamboo Forest Fishing Village," "Cloud Emerging," "Empty Smoke," "Lin'an Mountain Scenery," "Yushan Jianmen Pass," "River and Sky Pavilion," "Taibai Watching the Spring," "Yunxi High Hermit," "Stream and Mountain Clearing Snow," "Autumn Mountain Thatched Hall," "Fuchun," and "Stream Pasture." Lifelike works are very rare. Could it be that he saw Wenmin's authentic work and then exerted himself to create it? The seller asked for six hundred gold pieces for this scroll. After returning it, I recorded its general appearance in this way to inform those who love antiquity.

Idle Talk on Storytelling 219

— Qingnan

For the past decade, storytellers from all over with a little bit of talent have gathered in Shanghai and lingered, not only those famous storytellers from the towns and villages of Songjiang, Taicang, Jiaxing, and Huzhou in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, but also those who fill the ranks of the Guangyu Society's hometown of Suzhou. Therefore, this year, Xia Hesheng, a member of the society who defected, performs in Suzhou, singing during the day on Lindun Road and at night in the Maoyuan in West City. At the beginning of his storytelling, he had more than four hundred listeners day and night, even with rumors that he made one thousand four or five hundred listeners. And the Maoyuan wall has crumbled under the squeeze; these rumors are all unfounded. It's like the saying "There are no great generals in Shu, so Liao Hua is the vanguard." How long ago it seemed like a flash of lightning, a moment of brilliance before extinguishing. Recently, when I went to Maoyuan again, I saw that the storyteller on the stage was still Xia Hesheng, but there were only seventy listeners below the stage. I was very surprised at the rise and fall of the storytelling career. There is so-called "momentum" and "tail end," but I have never seen such a disparity. I then studied with the old listeners. The main reason is that Xia's art has not yet reached a perfect state, so he lacks a lasting appeal. Secondly, the listeners at Xia's most prosperous time were mostly people of the opposite sex and from the lower and middle classes, with impure character. Once they encountered wind, rain, or obstacles, or the story's cliffhanger was declared a pause, the audience stopped coming and never recovered. It could not be like Zhang Buyun, He Yunfei, etc., who were successful and failed three times. The more the story went on, the more crowded the audience became. I don't know if Xia has also been guilty of divine intent, storing his mind to practice hard and strive to follow in Zhang and He's footsteps, hoping to wash away the shame of this uneven beginning and end. Li Bokang, a member of the Runyu Society in Shanghai, who sings Yang Naiwu, is also one of the most popular storytellers in recent years, because his unique ability to tell the strange story can be done by only one person and there is no split. His father, Li Wenbin, not only spoke with a strong Zhejiang accent, but also could not play the stringed instrument. Some people gave him the eight-character rating of "unpleasant appearance, tasteless language," but he still managed to win the favor of some people with this book. At that time, the Mao'er Opera troupe of the Qunxian Tea Garden immediately hired someone to introduce them and spent some money to buy his plot to compose and perform a new fashion opera, let alone the current Bokang, whose accent is flawed but much better than his father, and his singing can also be called above average. Naturally, his career is booming and he is carrying glory everywhere. However, the listeners that Bokang attracts suffer from the same problems as Xia Hesheng in Suzhou. In addition, he himself can only perform the roles of young men and women. When it comes to people in the latter part of the book, such as Xia Tongshan and Yang Changjun, their square robes and large sleeves, and the righteous men of Huang Jinman, their accents are either vulgar and uneducated or their behavior is rude, and they are not accepted by connoisseurs.

Note: There is still a section of this report that was mistakenly typeset after the "Mongolian and Manchu Gossip Record" in yesterday's newspaper (that is, the section about being able to compete with Li Bokang in recent years). Therefore, because this article was typeset at the same time, this section was mistakenly attached after the "Mongolian and Manchu Gossip Record." This is a special correction.

Storytelling Rotary Club

Three Eras (14) 220

— Zhang Henshui

(8) No More Sour Plum Drink

A week later, the policeman was indeed promoted to sergeant. Not knowing why Division Commander Zhang had promoted him, he took some time to come to the Division Commander Zhang's mansion on Nongshangbu Street to thank him in person. It was May again, and the locust trees in the whole alley were growing lush and green. The sun shone on the treetops, scattering green shade all over the ground. A sour plum drink seller, carrying his load, walked into the small alley next to him under the green shade. Reaching a white powder wall in the small alley, he rested his load again. Behind the white powder wall was a red building. Beneath the red building was a grape trellis, and Zhang Xiaosan's second concubine was sitting in a rattan chair under the grape trellis, enjoying the cool air. Zhang Xiaosan, dressed in silk clothes, also sat beside her, joking with the concubine. Suddenly, a shout arose from outside the wall. The voice first said a Beijing phrase, "Drink up!" Then it sang, "Osmanthus sugar, a lot of it, sweet and cool and delicious!" Finally, it added another Beijing phrase, "Drink up!" The second concubine smiled and said, "I heard that Beijing's sour plum drink is delicious. Let me try it." Zhang Xiaosan said, "The famous sour plum drink in Beijing isn't sold at the door. It's Xin Yuan Qi's from Changdian. They boil whole vats of it the year before and bury it in the soil to get through the winter. You can buy a small bottle for a dollar. If you want to drink it, I'll have someone buy a bottle. You can't drink what's sold at the door. Who knows what kind of water they boil it with? The black sugar and ice cubes are捞ed from the moat in the winter. It's full of feces and urine. You're sure to get diarrhea if you eat it." As he spoke, the shouting rose again outside the wall, "Osmanthus sugar, a lot of it, sweet and cool and delicious!" The second concubine frowned and said, "I want to sleep for a while. This sound keeps calling. How annoying! Can you stop him from calling?" Zhang Xiaosan quickly called the old maid to go outside and tell him. The old maid told the messenger, the messenger told the gatekeeper, and the gatekeeper told the policeman at the door. The policeman, along with the sergeant who had come to thank him, came to the small alley and said to the sour plum drink seller, "Hey, stop shouting here. Division Commander Zhang's bedroom is right behind the wall." The sour plum drink seller, seeing the sergeant and policeman coming together, dared not say more. He picked up his load and left, muttering in his mouth, "Officials always make trouble for the common people. They don't even allow calling where he sleeps. This business is hard to do. I'm going to join the army." (The End)

Social News Submission Guidelines 221

(1) Texts should be about domestic and foreign science, industry, commerce, rural areas.

(2) News about health, aviation, exploration, customs, or urban life is limited. Pictures are limited to various lyrical paintings about social life.

(3) Photos of the seasons, scenery, plants and animals, people, and news photography are acceptable. Photos of beautiful women in seasonal scenery are especially welcome.

(4) The number of words in each text should not exceed two thousand.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write manuscripts horizontally, do not write illegibly. Western texts should be avoided if possible, and if it is unavoidable to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not use blue ink to draw pictures, and do not use colored paper. Use white paper and black lines.

(8) Please indicate "Social News Editorial Department" when submitting manuscripts.

(9) All submissions will not be returned, whether published or not. If you need to return them, you should declare it in advance and attach sufficient postage.

(10) Remuneration: three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan for every thousand characters. Pictures and special photos will also be paid according to this example.

Other fees will be calculated separately for unique manuscripts.

Book and Newspaper Introduction Submission Guidelines 222

(1) Texts are limited to introducing the latest domestic and foreign publications. In addition to literary works, all books and newspapers on politics, economics, law, science, etc., are included. Unremarkable books and newspapers will not be introduced.

(2) Pictures are limited to domestic and foreign new works, recent works, and illustrations related to the text.

(3) Texts on textual research or research on ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(4) Pictures and photos are limited to those related to the text.

(5) The maximum number of words per text is three thousand.

(6) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(7) Do not use blue ink to draw pictures, and do not use colored paper. Use white paper and black lines.

(8) Please indicate "Book and Newspaper Introduction Editor" when submitting manuscripts.

(9) All submissions will not be returned, whether published or not. If you need to return them, you should declare it in advance and attach sufficient postage.

(10) Remuneration: three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand characters. Pictures and photos will also be paid according to this example. Other fees will be calculated separately for unique manuscripts.

Youth Garden

Revelry 223

— Ke Er

It was Saturday afternoon, and the dormitory was as quiet as death. Painting boxes, violins, and other things lay scattered in the corners, as if they were sleeping. In three days, this semester would be over. Friends who had homes to go to were all preparing to pack and leave, busy saying goodbye to their lovers and joining fellow villagers to spend this terrible hot summer in the warm embrace of their hometowns. Because they were about to have a small separation from Shanghai, they should at least take a stroll in the movie theater, park, or perhaps on the road, for that last moment of nostalgia. Who would stay in the dormitory and sulk?

The moldy rain, like an old woman's annoying nagging, like a festering sore, sowed the seeds of pain and annoyance on the earth. The noise of the neighbors penetrated the humid air. Rickshaws crushed the coal cinder of Changchun Road in the rain, making a rustling sound. Ah, depression and sorrow constantly attacked the heart of the wanderer. Perhaps he was gazing at the misty, gray sky on the terrace, or perhaps he was lying in bed thinking about something. Although he was flipping through a book at random, only line after line of printed characters floated before his eyes. Suddenly, a bright spark burst, and a fellowship invitation fell from the book.

"At 6:00 PM on June 20th, the Sixth Research Comrades' Fellowship will be held at the Dentholmo Hotel. You are cordially invited to attend..."

Wasn't it? Lao Huang told me yesterday to go earlier. It was already 5:45. Go ahead, go share a cup of happiness with some people.

In the tram, I thought that the joy I had hoped for for a long time would be realized immediately, and I thought of the institute and everything that had happened to the students in the past.

Our spirit of painting is calm and upward. Of course, it is commendable in the vertical aspect, but there is too little connection in the horizontal aspect. We are estranged and scattered, and no one understands anyone. In order to hope to dispel the barriers between classmates, so it was in the late spring that a few classmates in our charcoal drawing room initiated the Spark Society. Unexpectedly, the fact gave us a great disappointment. Although the classmates participated, they were not very enthusiastic. The biggest reason was that we could not make the classmates absolutely without doubt. Then there was Brother Tong's illness. Lao Huang and Xiao Rong were busy with their affairs. I also went to other places for some other events. The declaration stood lonely on the bulletin board and became increasingly haggard. Our organization was declared abortive. But the blame should still be borne by us initiators. Why is the will so fragile and the perseverance so lacking?

Artists, please poke your heads out of the ivory tower. Many attendees have gathered in Dentholmo. Misses are squeezing their bodies in narrow silk. Their lips are crimson, their hair is curled. The guys constantly pay attention to their new suits, fearing that they will accidentally be stained with dust or stepped on by others. Their polished leather shoes! Ah, beautiful lines, imaginative colors, undulating under dreamlike lights. Lao Xia and Lao Huang are busy greeting and arranging. Brother Zhong Da came despite his illness (?). We are really unspeakably happy.

6:40,

Chairman Fang Xuegu gave the opening speech,

Mr. Chen Qiucao reported on the establishment of the Research Institute,

The chairman introduced Mr. Hua Lin's speech, followed by a burst of warm applause.

Isn't Mr. Hua Lin a scholar who is very knowledgeable in art theory? We feel very fortunate and grateful that he took the time to come to us today. He talked about the Italian Renaissance and the artist's tireless search for comfort, giving us a fresh revelation and a correct understanding of art. His attitude is sincere and earnest, and his words are active and profound. Unfortunately, no one took shorthand. It is a great loss to ourselves and to friends who did not participate in this gathering. Mr. Hua Lin promised us that he would be very willing to talk to us when he had the opportunity in the future. We believe that Mr. Hua Lin is not just saying it.

Brother Tong is really a genius of humor. An ordinary sentence turns around in his brain and is broadcast from his mouth, immediately becoming funny and thought-provoking. But no matter how much others laugh, he still keeps a straight face and doesn't move a muscle. Although he came despite his illness today, his enthusiasm is still unabated. He not only teases the guys, but also refuses to let go of the misses. When Shao Guanghong's harmonica solo was over, he stood up to introduce Mr. Xi, portraying his resume vividly, and insisted that Mr. Xi sing a Hangzhou tune.

A burst of applause and laughter,

Friends, perhaps you have not admired Mr. Xi's demeanor. Hey, when he stands up to speak, covering his mouth with a handkerchief, shaking his waist, and speaking in a shrill voice, the misses can't help but smile when they see him.

Lao Huang's magic is not a waist-cutting beauty, but a waist-cutting thumb.

A Bing's magic is not water circulation, but water.

Oh, we forgot that Miss Pan's foreign songs are sung very well. When we run past the palace every day after class, wisps of trembling singing constantly penetrate from the window holes, circling alone on the palm trees. Ah, that tortuous note, that intoxicating melody, is really delicious.

Brother Tong is responsible for pulling and urging people.

Although after several enthusiastic applause and urging, after all, Eastern women have not yet extracted the quality of shyness. Everyone's palms are sore from clapping, and they can only get Miss Pan's few euphemistic and charming excuses.

There are more and more proposals. Brother Tong, the temporary chairman of the entertainment department, is too busy to eat. Finally, the mentors were also swept into the vortex. But after all, the old foxes are resourceful. When they have no way to perfunctory anymore, they reach into their arms and take out a brocade bag of wonderful plans. They clap their eyes open and the smoke fills the entire dining room. Instantaneous light photography, the last program.

Happiness filled every cell in our bodies, and white wings were drawn from our shoulders. Ah, flying in the starry sky.

Book and Newspaper Introduction

Municipal Administration of Four Major Cities: Beijing, Shanghai, Hangzhou, and Hankou 226

— Tang Bin

By Dong Xiujia

European and American countries attach great importance to municipal administration. If municipal administration is not developed, it will hinder the country's resources and social order. In recent years, the National Government in my country has also paid great attention to the reform of municipal administration during the construction period, striving for the new development of each city. It has either sent special personnel to Europe and the United States for inspection or conducted detailed investigations in the country to learn from municipal administration. The four major cities of Beijing, Shanghai, Hangzhou, and Hankou hold the nation's pivot, and their administrative facilities should be systematically investigated as a comparative study of domestic municipal administration. By discarding its shortcomings and taking its strengths, the development of municipal administration will not be far off. Only the governments of Beijing, Shanghai, and Hangzhou are the most important because their institutions are complex and their undertakings are numerous. The Nanjing City Government is divided into six bureaus: Public Works, Finance, Health, Social Affairs, Education, and Land, as well as the Secretariat and the Council Chamber. The Shanghai City Government is divided into bureaus of Public Works, Finance, Public Security, Health, Social Affairs, Education, Public Utilities, Port Affairs, and Land, as well as the Secretariat and the Council Chamber. The Shanghai Public Concession Engineering Bureau and the French Concession Engineering Bureau are also divided into multiple offices. The Hangzhou City Government is divided into three bureaus: Public Security, Public Works, and Finance, as well as four sections: Land, Education, Social Affairs, and Health. However, scholars studying municipal administration must have a detailed understanding of such municipal conditions. This entire facility should be explored and compared with the methods of these three cities to serve as a reference for improving other cities. The author, in view of this and as his own responsibility, has this investigation of municipal administration, detailing the special advantages of the four major cities and attaching his own views on improving municipal administration for researchers or responsible persons to adopt. Although the points presented are generally methods that major European and American cities have implemented for a long time and have achieved effective results, they are also methods that major cities in my country urgently need to emulate. Therefore, this kind of municipal administration investigation report is of great concern to the future of municipal administration in cities throughout the country, and the value of this book can also be seen in this. As for the author being a municipal administration expert, there is no need to introduce him here.

The whole book is divided into nine chapters. The first chapter is general affairs. In order to make it systematic, the author will describe it using inductive methods. General affairs include municipal governments and their various bureaus, offices, and sections, and matters of a public nature, such as office procedures, file management systems, employment methods, attendance methods, statistical compilation, propaganda methods, saving supplies, joint office work, and the abolition of the first section of each bureau, centralized procurement, and other issues. The most prominent of these is the plan for the period of political tutelage, which the municipal government should also pay attention to. The author has included all those that should be considered to belong to general affairs in this general affairs chapter for discussion. Office procedures are to explain the order of handling affairs in an agency, based on the regulations or general rules of an agency, and to draw up a guide for employees to handle affairs, which is most beneficial for handling affairs and especially useful for new employees of an agency. Now, in order to avoid errors in handling affairs and reduce them, cities in various countries explain the procedures for handling affairs to new employees at any time, so there is a paper on office procedures suspended in the office of each agency. Its method is excellent. Most of the major cities in my country have adopted this method, which shows that the progress of municipal administration cannot be measured. Although this is a very common thing, scholars who truly study municipal administration need to investigate its situation in detail.

Secondly, methods of municipal administration propaganda are also important. The citizens not only need to understand the things that the city is doing, but also translate the precedents of things done by cities in various countries into vernacular language, print them into pamphlets, and distribute them to the citizens, so that the public knows that all countries pay great attention to municipal construction and that the municipal administration methods currently in effect in my country have all been implemented by various countries long ago. The other reliance on daily newspaper municipal administration weekly publications to promote municipal administration speeches is also important. All undertakings that want to start and seek full development must pay attention to the various working methods described above. Therefore, the practical municipal administration plan for the six-year period of political tutelage can be realized.

"The municipal administration plan for the period of political tutelage is to be completed in six years, and orders were issued to the provinces and cities to carry out the undertakings that should be carried out during the period of political tutelage in six years (and to carry out the undertakings that should be carried out during the period of political tutelage in a planned manner year by year, so that constitutional government can be implemented in accordance with the Prime Minister's will from the 24th year of the Republic of China. This time, I went to the cities of Beijing, Shanghai, and Hangzhou to inspect municipal administration and saw that Hangzhou was preparing for village, neighborhood, and community autonomy. Nanjing was also studying the division of autonomous regions. Shanghai Special City also entrusted committees from various cities and townships to actively prepare for the autonomous affairs of cities and townships. Our city specially presented to the central government for approval to organize a temporary council for the cultivation of self-government. This is because we feel that the time for political tutelage is very short and we cannot but prepare in advance for the autonomous undertakings during the period of constitutional government. The method of preparing in advance is excellent. However, in addition to the training of people's self-government that has already been prepared in various cities, it seems that there is no concrete plan for the work that should be done during the period of political tutelage. ... My intention is that everything will be established in advance. Since the central government has set the period of political tutelage for six years, each bureau of our city should pre-set the work of political tutelage for six years and complete it annually. ... Therefore, since the work of each bureau of the city government has a certain standard, the citizens of the entire city can also understand the work of the city government year by year, and the constitutional government can be implemented when the constitutional government begins." We can see from the above that the municipal administration plan for the period of political tutelage is extremely important. If it is carried out step by step and improved year by year, then the day when my country's municipal administration wants to keep pace with Europe and the United States is not far off.

Chapter 2: Public Works. This includes many issues, including the issue of surveying the entire city, the issue of main roads throughout the city, the issue of roadbeds, the issue of selecting road materials, the issue of the city's administrative district plan, the issue of land acquisition prices and road construction fees, the design committee, and the issue of planning the entire city of Hankou. The author discusses these in detail in separate sections.

Chapter 3: Public Administration. This chapter covers a very large scope, but during this investigation of the administration of the three cities of Beijing, Shanghai, and Hangzhou, the author paid special attention to the following five issues in public administration: the establishment of electrical testing laboratories, the reorganization of street lights, advertising issues, the installation of traffic lights, and the issues of trams and buses. These are described in detail in this chapter.

Chapter 4: Social Administration. This includes three categories: agriculture, industry, commerce, and labor-management issues, charitable undertakings. Its scope is very large and its responsibilities are very heavy. Even if it is handled properly, its achievements are not seen, which is completely different from public works administration or public administration. This kind of administration is a term recently created in my country's law, which combines the agriculture, industry, commerce bureau and the public welfare bureau administration stipulated in the previous law into one. The intention of this kind of combined administration method is to reduce administrative expenses and transfer them to business expenses, which is very good. However, because the scope of administration is too large, it is not easy to handle. This time, the author went to the cities of Beijing, Shanghai, and Hangzhou to investigate municipal administration. He paid special attention to social administration and was greatly concerned about the reorganization and promotion of agriculture, industry, commerce, labor-management disputes, unemployment relief, civic housing, charitable undertakings, and other issues in each city. The development of urban construction undertakings is closely related to agriculture, industry, and commerce. If agriculture, industry, and commerce cannot develop, the city government's income will not improve, and the urban construction undertakings will not be revitalized. Secondly, labor-management disputes have become the most troublesome issue in modern cities. All cities should pay special attention to them. For example, imperialists are destroying my country's laborers, causing various storms that have a great impact on local security. Therefore, the Social Affairs Bureau must conduct in-depth research on the issue of labor-management disputes, while still following the Prime Minister's will of labor-management harmony, striving to promote labor-management cooperation so that laborers will not be misled by malignant forces, and capital can improve the treatment of workers within the scope of their abilities. The next issue is the issue of unemployment, which is also the most important issue in cities around the world. In the cities of various countries, there is still no considerable solution. It is especially important in my country to try to provide relief. The other items have been stated separately by the author and will not be repeated here.

There are also educational administration, health administration, public security administration, port administration, financial administration, and land administration. The author has described what he has learned in detail. During the period of political tutelage and construction, such a special book comparing the municipal administration of major cities is rare. Since the publication of this book, it will have a great impact on the progress of various municipal administrations in my country, and the points discussed in this book have been adopted and implemented in the city of Hankou, which has discovered unique effects. The value of this book can be seen from this.

Children's Club 227

— Tang Bin

Inaugural Issue Published by Joint Bookstore

Recently, a good phenomenon has been emerging in the Chinese publishing world, which is paying attention to the publication of children's books, increasing elementary school students' interest in reading, and guiding them to proper entertainment, preventing them from reading all kinds of useless and bad books. Moreover, these books should not be aimed at profit in bookstores, but should strive for low prices to reduce the burden on children, and should not exploit children as much as books for college or middle school students. Otherwise, it would hinder the future of children's education. Now I want to recommend to readers this "Children's Club", seeing that its publishing purpose is to cope with this environment and produce a publication. Its content is suitable for elementary school students in the fourth, fifth, and sixth grades. There is no need to worry about being too profound or too superficial, and it adopts the strengths of various publications to innovate, striving for new and correct ideas in writing, and guiding children to a bright path as a vital force in the reform of children's education.

At the same time, elementary school students' thoughts are very simple. If they are properly trained and cultivated, they can easily embark on a meaningful life path. However, cultivating their ability to read and appreciate is also extremely important. What do they really do every day? They go to school to listen to teachers and play with friends, and return home to help their families with small tasks. These things are too annoying. If they are called to entertainment venues, it is of course most appropriate to allow them to read this "Children's Club", as the editor said in the "Meeting" section of this publication:

"In this small entertainment venue, someone tells you stories, someone tells you jokes, someone teaches you new ways to play, there are truths you can't hear in the classroom, and there are funs you can't get at home. There are also beautiful pictures that surpass natural scenery, and clear and wonderful music and elegant singing that are no less than the performances and singing in dance halls, and there are endless and inexhaustible varieties of juggling and amusement, making you want to listen and watch and play until you dream of your mother's side. What a fun entertainment venue this is! Children, please come, please come quickly to this wonderful entertainment venue!"

"Children, as you play in this entertainment venue every day, your wisdom can increase day by day, your body can become stronger day by day, and your character can become more noble day by day. You will find it more interesting to listen to lectures in the classroom, and you will have more fun playing with friends. When you return home and talk to your older and younger brothers, older and younger sisters, they will admire and respect you all the more. See how beneficial this entertainment venue is to you!"

These words have considerable significance. If children's literature is founded in accordance with such pure principles, of course, it will not

Page 22

make any mistakes. Cultivating children's reading habits is ten thousand times more noble than fathers and elder brothers taking them into improper entertainment venues. The stories, fairy tales, etc. collected here pay attention to both fun and thought, and instill in them a lot of world literature and music knowledge. For example, Hu Zhaoshu's "Why Should We Learn Music?" is a clear exposition. At the beginning, the author explains the five reasons why we should learn music: (1) Music can make our bodies healthy; (2) Music can make our minds happy; (3) Music is a good social skill; (4) Music is the best kind of education; (5) Music is a tool that makes us move forward. This saying is of course very appropriate. Music can make individuals move forward, and considering the entire society, it can also make the entire society move forward. Because of this, children have a reason to learn music. Secondly, there is the same author's biography of the world musician Ludwig Van Beethoven, which describes his life and musical talent in extremely simple language. Children can certainly benefit a lot from reading such a biography. At least in terms of general knowledge, it can be enriched. Even we adults can benefit from reading it. Moreover, if the biography of a celebrity is recorded in history, then we cannot get a deep memory from reading it. This is a reading experience. Reading a biography here, in addition to arousing infinite interest, can also gain some musical knowledge, which is really valuable.

The "Science World" column is also very valuable. For example, Fu Zhenshi's telephone, the wireless telephone that others cannot hear, robots driving airplanes, electric typewriters, fish also drowning, and airplanes protecting fruit trees are all works that stimulate children's intelligence and increase their inspiration for invention. The author's writing is mainly based on fun, so we don't feel the dryness and boredom of reading other science books when we read some of them. Moreover, the narrative strives to be concise and does not contain any empty words, but in this extremely short description, children can get a lot of so-called scientific knowledge.

"Peach Blossom's Song" is full of infinite poetic flavor. The author strives to refine the rhymes so that readers can sing easily, but there is no affectation or reduction of the clear and simple poetic essence. Poetry originally contains mystery, which of course cannot be the case here. It must be mainly for children to understand, so this type of poetry looks clear and simple on the surface, as if it was written by people who do not have sufficient literary cultivation. In fact, it is necessary to consider various difficult problems, such as being easy to sing and easy to understand, which is really not easy to express so precisely. This "Peach Blossom's Song" can be said to be a model of children's poetry.

Others such as Xie Liuyi's "Hen and Chicks," Ying'er and Jiang Heng's "Rabbit's Cotton Tail and Big Turtle" are all extremely valuable masterpieces. When we read them, we can understand that they are written by people who have full literary cultivation, not as beautifully as ordinary people who create children's literature can write. Therefore, children's literature is not an easy work to create. At the same time, in today's era when young people's thoughts are unusually divergent, children's literature cannot be ignored.
